## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillators)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration of a (nonlinear) oscillator, typically modeled by second-order ODEs where acceleration depends on restoring forces from x, damping/friction from v, and possible external/parametric forcing via t. Common sub-models include Duffing, Van der Pol/LiÃ©nard-type oscillators, and driven/damped harmonic motion.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic restoring force: dv_dt = -c0 * x (undamped simple harmonic oscillator)
- Linear damping + restoring: dv_dt = -c0 * v - c1 * x (viscous damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * v - c1 * x + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (sinusoidal external drive)
- Nonlinear (cubic) stiffness / Duffing (unforced): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (forced nonlinear resonance)
- Pendulum-type restoring force: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (large-angle oscillations; periodic potential)
- Quadratic (turbulent) drag: dv_dt = -c0 * v * Abs(v) - c1 * x (drag magnitude grows ~v^2)
- Dry/Coulomb friction (smooth approximation): dv_dt = -c0 * v / (Abs(v) + c1) - c2 * x (velocity-sign-like friction near constant magnitude)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (c1 - x**2) * v - c2 * x (self-excited oscillations; nonlinear damping)
- General LiÃ©nard-type polynomial damping: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**4) * v - c3 * x (amplitude-dependent dissipation)
- Parametric (Mathieu-like) excitation: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (time-varying stiffness; parametric resonance)
- Time-varying damping: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * v - c3 * x (periodically modulated dissipation)
- Piecewise/hardening symmetric stiffness via absolute value: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * Abs(x) * x - c2 * v (stiffness increases with |x|)
- Polynomial potential expansion (odd restoring): dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5) - c3 * v (anharmonic oscillator from Taylor-expanded potential)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative oscillator structure: if dv_dt depends only on x (no v, no t), dynamics often conserve an energy-like quantity and produce closed phase-plane orbits.
- Restoring-force symmetry: many mechanical oscillators have odd restoring forces (dv_dt is odd in x), suggesting terms like -x, -x**3, -sin(c*x), or -Abs(x)*x.
- Nonlinear stiffness signatures: adding -c * x**3 (or higher odd powers) yields amplitude-dependent frequency (hardening/softening), a key indicator of Duffing-like behavior.
- Viscous damping: linear -c * v produces exponential decay of amplitude for small oscillations and monotone energy loss per cycle.
- Nonlinear damping/friction: terms like -v*Abs(v) or -v/(Abs(v)+c) indicate drag/friction whose magnitude grows superlinearly or saturates near a constant, altering decay rate with amplitude.
- Self-excitation/limit cycles: factors multiplying v that change sign with x (e.g., (c - x**2)*v) indicate negative damping at small amplitude and positive damping at large amplitude, producing stable limit cycles.
- External periodic forcing: additive terms depending only on t (e.g., cos(c*t), sin(c*t)) suggest driven resonance, beats, and possible chaos when combined with nonlinearity.
- Parametric excitation: time-dependent stiffness multiplying x (e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x) is characteristic of Mathieu-type instability tongues and parametric resonance.
- State-dependent dissipation: damping coefficients that depend on x (e.g., (c0 + c1*x**2)*v) imply dissipation varies over the cycle, often modeling geometry-dependent drag or nonlinear material effects.
- Near-equilibrium small-angle limit: sin(c*x) â‰ˆ c*x links pendulum-like models to linear SHO behavior; observing a transition from sinusoidal to linear forms indicates operating regime.
